<!DOCTYPE html PUBLIC "-//W3C//DTD XHTML 1.0 Transitional//EN" "http://www.w3.org/TR/xhtml1/DTD/xhtml1-transitional.dtd"><html xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><head ><title>Transit Agencies Providing GTFS Data - Table Format</title><link rel="stylesheet" href="/static/style.css" type="text/css" media="all" /><link rel="alternate" type="application/rss+xml" title="Atom" href="/feed" /></head><body><div id="container"><div id="dashboard"></div><div id="header"><h1><a href="/" ><img src="/static/logo.png" alt="GTFS Data Exchange" width="143" height="61"></a></h1><div class="shutdown"><h2>Notice: GTFS Data Exchange Shutting Down</h2><p>I <a href="https://jehiah.cz/a/why-to-share-public-transit-data">started</a> GTFS Data Exchange in 2008 to encourage adoption of the GTFS specification when barely a dozen transit agencies were sharing schedule data. Since then, much has changed as there are over a thousand agencies from almost every country around the world publishing GTFS data.</p><p>Recently the Secretary of the US DOT wrote a letter <a href="http://gis.rita.dot.gov/Transit/downloads/DearColleague.pdf">advocating broad GTFS contribution</a> and a national registry of GTFS, coming one step shy of requiring it from all agencies. The World Bank has also heavily <a href="https://github.com/WorldBank-Transport/GTFS-Training-Materials/wiki/Link-repository-for-international-GTFS-training-materials">advocated and assisted international adoption of GTFS</a>. That these sorts of organizations have a default expectation of open schedule data was unthinkable in 2008. I'm proud of all the transit community has accomplished, and excited about what's next. Closing gtfs-data-exchange will pave the way for the next chapter of open transit data.</p><h3>What's next for the Transit Community? </h3><p><a href="https://transit.land/">https://transit.land/</a> has steadily been growing as a reference spot for worldwide GTFS data, and the spot for transit agencies to connect with developers. It is also built to expose schedule data from a single consistent database which makes it even easier for developers to access schedule information. Most importantly though, Transitland has a corporate sponsor <a href="https://mapzen.com/">Mapzen</a>, so developers can rely on it whereas gtfs-data-exchange has always been a side project, intermittently available and sometimes neglected.</p><p><a href="http://transitfeeds.com/">http://transitfeeds.com/</a> also has a comprehensive list of GTFS feeds, and is built on a much more open and transparent community contribution process via Github.</p><h3>Timeline for shutting down GTFS Data Exchange:</h3><ul><li><strong>April 1, 2016</strong> - Feed registry and file uploads disabled</li><li><strong>May 1, 2016</strong> - Automatic feed updates disabled</li><li><strong>July 1, 2016</strong> - API access to feeds disabled.</li><li><strong>Sept 1, 2016</strong> - GTFS-Data-Exchange will switch to a minimal index of agencies</li></ul><h3>Frequently Asked Questions:</h3><p><strong>Q:</strong> Where should I register a transit agency's feed?<br/><strong>A:</strong> <a href="https://transit.land/feed-registry/">https://transit.land/feed-registry/</a> and <a href="https://github.com/TransitFeeds/TransitFeeds-Public/issues">https://github.com/TransitFeeds/TransitFeeds-Public/issues</a></p><p><strong>Q:</strong> What will happen to historical feeds on gtfs-data-exchange?</br><strong>A:</strong> Historic feed archive will be available for research via <a href="http://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/RequesterPaysBuckets.html">AWS S3 "requestor pays" policy</a>. The dataset is currently 13k files totaling 93G from 2008 onward. Contact me if you'd like access.</p><hr><p>A special thanks to the fine folks at <a href="http://trilliumtransit.com/">TrilliumTransit</a>, and <a href="https://www.walkscore.com/">WalkScore</a> for their support and encouragement over the years.</p><p>If you have any specific questions about this transitio, reach out to me <a href="https://twitter.com/jehiah">@jehiah</a></p></div></div><div id="nav"><div id="usernav"><a href="/upload" >Upload GTFS File</a> <span class="pipe">|</span><a href="https://www.google.com/accounts/ServiceLogin?service=ah&passive=true&continue=https://appengine.google.com/_ah/conflogin%3Fcontinue%3Dhttp://www.gtfs-data-exchange.com/agencies/astable" >Sign In</a></div><a href="/agencies">All Agencies</a> <span class="pipe">|</span><a href="/">Recent Updates</a></div><div id="body"><h2>Transit Agencies Providing GTFS Data</h2><p>View: <a href="/agencies">by Agency</a> <span class="pipe">|</span><a href="/agencies/bylocation">by Location</a> <span class="pipe">|</span><a href="/agencies/bylastupdate" >by Last Update</a> <span class="pipe">|</span><a href="/agencies/astable" class="selected">as Table</a></p><p id="filters">Filter: <a href="#filter_all" id="filter_all" class="selected" >All Sources</a> <span class="pipe">|</span> <a href="#filter_official" id="filter_official">Official Sources</a></p><p>Data is Available for 1000 Transit Agencies.</p><p> <a href="/feed"><img src="/static/feed.png" border="0" align="absbottom"> RSS of All Updates</a></p><hr><table class="datatable" celpadding="2" cellspacing="0"><tr><th>Agency</th><th>Location</th><th>Feed Source</th><th>License Agreement</th><th>Last Update</th></tr><tr class="unofficial"><td><img src="/static/star_grey.png" width="17" height="22" alt="No Offical GTFS Data Source Available" title="No Offical GTFS Data Source Available" align="absbottom"><a href="/agency/a-reich-gmbh-busbetrieb/">A. &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<img src="/static/star_grey.png" width="17" height="22" alt="No Offical GTFS Data Source Available" title="No Offical GTFS Data Source Available" align="absbottom"> No Offical GTFS Data Source Available</p><hr><h3>How to Provide Open Data</h3><p>1) Publish your schedule data as a <a href="http://code.google.com/transit/spec/transit_feed_specification.html">GTFS</a> feed. Google publishes <a href="http://maps.google.com/help/maps/transit/partners/participate.html">instructions</a> on how to create GTFS feeds.</p><p>2) Provide an official URL where your feed can be downloaded. This can be a URL on your agency site or a URL to a third-party authorized to host your feed. Note: a simple way to provide an official URL is to <a href="/upload">upload your feed</a> to GTFS Data Exchange and use the provided url. </p><p>3) Send email to <a href="http://groups.google.com/group/transit-developers">transit-developers@googlegroups.com</a> with the URL of your feed. Note: this is a public mailing list.</p><p>4) <a href="/submit-feed">Submit GTFS feed location</a> for inclusion on GTFS Data Exchange. This helps developers find the URL where your data is published.</p><hr/><p>Is your local transit agency missing from GTFS Data Exchange? Please contact them directly and ask that they make their data available to their riders. A list of agencies and their contacts can be found at <a href="http://www.citygoround.org/agencies/">www.citygoround.org</a></p><div class="clear"></div></div><div id="footer"><h3>API</h3><p>GTFS Data Exchange <a href="/api">API Documentation</a></p><h3>Resources</h3><ul><li><a href="http://code.google.com/transit/spec/transit_feed_specification.html">GTFS Specification</a></li><li><a href="/how-to-provide-open-data">How to Provide Open Data</a></li><li><a href="http://groups.google.com/group/transit-developers">Transit Developers Discussion Group</a></li><li><a href="http://groups.google.com/group/gtfs-changes">GTFS Specification Discussion Group</a></li><li><a href="http://groups.google.com/group/gtfs-changes/web/open-proposals">Proposed GTFS Specification Changes</a></li><li><a href="http://code.google.com/p/googletransitdatafeed/wiki/FeedValidator">GTFS Feed Validator</a></li></ul><h3>About GTFS Data Exchange</h3><p>This site is designed to help developers and transit agencies efficiently share and retrieve GTFS data. GTFS-data-exchange helps eliminate the time between feed publication by a transit agency and when the developer is alerted to it's presence. This is accomplished by per-agency RSS feeds that developers and other GTFS consumers subscribe to.</p><p>This Site has been designed by <a href="http://jehiah.cz/">Jehiah Czebotar</a> along with feedback from the GTFS community.<br/>For updates about this site, follow <a href="http://twitter.com/gtfs_data">@gtfs_data</a>.</p><p>Data posted on this site is provided AS IS.
